Feature Match Round 3 – Adam Barnello vs. Pascal Maynard
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Brian David-Marshall* 

Adam Barnello is a **Magic** columnist who took part in the Legacy roundtable that appeared in my weekly article and -- with bonus footage -- in the coverage for this event. To keep with a time-honored tradition of covering **Magic** authors in last round before all the Pros start to show up with their hard fought byes expired and Barnello got the call in Providence.


Barnello was playing the blue-white deck that many of the pros wearing ChannelFireball shirts were apparently very high on. In addition to all the control staples that make up the Legacy format it dips into the Standard pool for [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) and its newest creation [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull).


His opponent was Pascal Maynard, who was one of the members of last year's Canadian National team that thrust [Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempered+Steel) into the Extended spotlight at the World Championships in Chiba. Maynard was not at all happy about his deck choice for this event.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm3.jpg)"My deck is very bad," he sighed out of ear shot from Barnello. "I should have registered anything else."


He was playing a blue-white merfolk deck that also featured everyone's favorite Mystic and an assortment of powerful equipment.


### Game 1


Both players kept their opening hands with Maynard on the play. The Quebecer tried [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept) -- revealing Rejeery -- only to have it was [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare)d for the first action of the game. Barnello had a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) for Mautavault and another a turn later when Maynard played his own [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and tapped it to pay for [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte).


Maynard was stuck on one land which he used to play [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) while [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) for [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) was going on over on Barnello's side of the table.


[Aether Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aether+Vial) was attempted a turn later but it drew [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will).


Barnello put a 4/4 vigilant life linked germ into play. He untapped and played [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor); when he reached for a die to mark the loyalty counters Pascal stopped him: "In response..."


And scooped up all three of his cards.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm3Barnello.jpg)*Adam Barnello*
### Game 2


The two players sideboarded with no chatter. Maynard no doubt quietly regretting his deck choice while Adam explained his silence: "Even after one game I can't shake the nervous jitters."


It was his first feature match but Maynard was experienced having been last featured in Atlanta. Turn one [Aether Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aether+Vial) from Maynard did not draw the dreaded [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep) from Barnello and the two players settled into their game. Adam [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ed [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) and Maynard untapped.


Adam [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed and tucked a couple pieces of equipment back on top of his deck. Maynard Vial'd in a [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept) and passed the turn back to Barnello after attacking with his Vial still on two and two lands in play.


Barnello shuffled back his two equipments with a fetch land and untapped to play Vedlaken [Shackles](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shackles). Maynard had the [Disenchant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disenchant) and then activated his Vial and Stoneforged for his own [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull).


He left the Vial on two and cracked for two with the Adept before playing [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) and passing the turn. Barnello passed the turn with no play and a germ joined his team. He used the Vial to put another Adept into play and Barnello played [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on one of them.


When Maynard activated his [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) another Swords showed up after a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) to stem the bleeding. Maynard played [Coralhelm Commander](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coralhelm+Commander) and leveled it up twice. When he tried to level it a third time on his next turn it drew a third Swords.


Maynard attacked and Barnello flashed in [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique). Maynard let it resolve and when Barnello targeted his opponent with the ability, the Canadian National team member used Vial to flash in [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis). Barnello did a little survey of the battlefield and conceded.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm3Maynard.jpg)*Pascal Maynard*
### Game 3


More silent shuffling as they moved toward finally getting the rubber game of the match underway. Neither player liked their opening seven and went back for six more cards after another round of silent shuffling. Barnello was not happy with his six-carder and sent it back in hopes of five cards he could work with.


[Aether Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aether+Vial) landed without a response from Barnello -- as did the second one that Maynard played a turn later. Barnello took advantage of a small window and attacked for two with his [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory).


Maynard used his first Vial on his own turn two to drop an uncounterable Commander and level it up twice.


Maynard fully leveled it a turn later and Vialed a Rejeery in play to take it even higher. Barnello untapped, searched for [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra) and Wrathed away Maynard's team. The Quebec player restocked with [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis) and Merrow Rejeery over the end of Barnello's turn and the main of his own.


Barnello dropped [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) for [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) and played [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) on Maynard's turn. The Quebecer played Forece of Will, discarding [Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misstep) to protect his last card. Barnello put the [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) into play at the end of Maynard's next turn and it was promptly [Disenchant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disenchant)ed.


Maynard was out of cards and Barnello was about to untap and play [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). Maynard sent his Rejeery into the red zone leaving his Lord of Atalntis back.


And then things got interesting.


Barnello cast [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on the [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis) that was granting [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)walk to the Rejeery. Barnello then used his Mystic to put another [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) into play. At this point a spectator stopped the game to get a judge because their was some confusion about how many lands Barnello had played. They all agreed that Barnello had played an extra land and they backed up the play. Barnello had to Swords the [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis) and then chump block with Mystic since he did not have enough mana to do both.


Barnello, who was still visibly nervous about playing in Feature Match


announced: "My land for the turn."


He then used the [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) ability of Jace and reflexively went to play another land which was immediately caught by everyone who had heard him announce his first land drop a few seconds back. The judge, who was still writing up the dual warnings from the previous infraction, added it to the list. Should Barnello pick up another warning on the day -- regardless of the infraction -- it would result in a game loss.


Barnello attacked for four and played yet another Mystic for yet another [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull). Maynard was not happy and Vial'd an Adept into play. He then hardcast a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) of his own. He was out of cards.


Barnello played Swords on the germ and attacked with his own [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) and [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory).


Maynard equipped his Adept and attacked Jace. Barnello chumped with Stoneforge which had summoning sickness and he untapped to play another Mystic -- this time fetching [Sword of Body and Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Body+and+Mind). He had enough mana at this point to simply play the Sword and attach it to his germ token. Maynard took six, milled 10, and Barnello started working on his wolf pack.


Time expired as Barnello passed the turn but with the remaining extra turns he was able to get through with his 10/10 vigilant, life linked, protection from blue, germ token for the win but he was not happy with the jitters he had displayed in doing so.


**Final result: Adam Barnello sheepishly won the match 2 - 1**




Feature Match Round 4 – Paul Rietzl vs. Brian Kibler
----------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

Sometimes, you're just handed a gimme. For me, picking this match was a gimme. For the players involved, getting their first actual win of the day was not. Paul Rietzl and Brian Kibler have been staples on the **Magic** scene for about as long as I can remember. They have literally done it all in **Magic**, getting just about every type of accolade you can imagine between them as **Magic** players. Having been around as long as they have, the two are good friends, and this match had a definite feel of joking comfortability to it. Rietzl even went so far as to take a page out of David Ochoa's book, declaring this a war of good versus evil. I'll let you guess what side he was on.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm4GvE.jpg)"Gotta rep it," Rietzl said taking his jacket off as he sat down to reveal his Your Move Games shirt underneath.


"Old school, eh," Kibler responded.


"99% of this room probably has no idea what this shirt even is," Rietzl joked.


"Yeah, I never thought that I'd be the elder statesman of anything,"Kibler laughed.


### Game 1


Kibler won the die roll and chose to go first.


Rietzl started the first turn with a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), peeling a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) from a hand also containing a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), [Vindicate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vindicate), and two [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)s. Apparently Kibler drew a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) for his turn, immediately aiming the conspicuously new card at Reitl's hand.


"That was probably the perfect card to draw," Rietzl said, sliding his hand onto the table.


Two copies of [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith), an [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte), [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), and two lands stared back at him. After merely a few seconds to record the info, Kibler sent the Swords packing.


Rietzl kept the land count minimal, using a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to kill Kibler's [Bayou](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bayou). Upon finally reaching a second and, Kibler made the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) he was holding, currently a 4/5. With a [Savannah](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Savannah) and a new [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) in his hand, Rietzl could simply Swords the Goyf, choosing instead to use a Zenith to fetch a matching copy of his own. When Kibler made a second copy for his team, Rietzl once again chose to let it be, clearly saving his Swords for the far more dangerous [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). Instead, he made and equipped an [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte), passing the turn in defense.


Kibler had no intention of smashing into the equipped Goyf. Instead, he made a freshly drawn [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), which fetched a [Sword of Fire and Ice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Fire+and+Ice). On his turn, needing to thin the board some, Rietzl sent his Goyf into Kibler's team. Kibler blocked with the whole team. Rietzl's Goyf died, but not before dealing enough to one of Kibler's for the Jitte to finish it off. After combat, Rietzl replaced it with the far more imposing [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary).


"Right on time," Kibler said triumphantly as he put a [Scrubland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scrubland) into play. A [Vindicate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vindicate) sent the Knight to its final resting place. Even with the board clear, Kibler chose not to attack, fearing an attack back from Rietzl's [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor). With Kibler only having two blockers, Rietzl chose to use a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to get rid of the Goyf, leaving just a Mystic behind. He then equipped his Arbor with the Jitte and sent it in Kibler took the damage, which let Rietzl use the Jitte to kill the Mystic before it could ever activate. On his turn, Kibler put Rietzl in some mana troubles, using [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to kill his [Savannah](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Savannah), his only source of white mana. In addition, he had finally gotten to the point when he could play his [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), giving him the largest creature on the board.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm4Kibler.jpg)*Brian Kibler*
Rietzl untapped and made a pair of [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)s, collectively larger than the [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). Kibler used a [Vindicate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vindicate) to get rid of the Jitte, bringing things to an absolute halt. Rietzl found a way to get the advantage the immediate next turn. [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) gave him the ability to dig for an answer, and, after talking himself through a tutorial on how to use top ("So I have to peek then draw…or do I draw then peek…I'll figure this out…"), he ended up putting a land into play and a mystery card on top.


Kibler couldn't attack, instead opting to draw some cards with some Horizon Canopies and his [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). Rietzl had a plan for his turn. It was time to turn up the heat. He attacked with his two [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)s. When Kibler blocked with his [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), Rietzl used his to search out a [Bojuka Bog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bojuka+Bog), erasing Kibler's graveyard and shrinking his Knight. Rather than lose the only way he could really get back into the game, Kibler chose to fetch up a white source with his Knight to cast a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) he'd blocked. Unfortunately, the Bog had put him so far behind that Rietzl's men only needed a couple more turns to overwhelm Kibler. Kibler aimed a last-second [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach) at Rietzl, hoping to just get a little more information.


Paul Rietzl 1 – Brian Kibler 0


### Game 2


"You have a major advantage right now," Rietzl said bobbing up and down.


"What's that," Kibler asked?


"I really have to go to the bathroom."


Kibler opened incredibly strongly in the second game. His first-turn [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) stripped a [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) from a hand containing a pair of [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach)s, a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), and a couple of lands. That cleared the way for his [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) to start cementing his advantage. Rietzl tried to stem the advantage with a [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach), but it wasn't really any match for [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant).


Kibler kept the aggro up, adding a second [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) to the board and using [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to put Rietzl off of double black. When a Knight hit the table a turn later, and Rietzl found hiself unable to cast any meaningful spells, the game was over. This lightning quick game was the antithesis of the first, with things going Kibler's way from the start and Rietzl never really even being in it.


Paul Rietzl 1 – Brian Kibler 1


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm4Rietzl.jpg)*Paul Rietz*
### Game 3


Rietzl ramped himself up with a first-turn [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for a [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor) which Kibler immediately [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ed. Kibler also made a [Mox Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Diamond), enabling him to play a [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) as well. He activated it on his upkeep, thinking for a while about how to order his cards. Rietzl had spent his second turn making a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), so Kibler had to take that into consideration. Eventually, he ordered his cards, activating his top after his draw for a second card. With his Top still on his deck, he cracked a [Verdant Catacombs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Verdant+Catacombs) to get a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp), allowing him to cast a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize). The sorcery stole a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) out of a hand containing a second [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), and a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Rietzl returned the favor on his turn, using his [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) to take a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) from a hand with [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) and [Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elspeth%2C+Knight-Errant). Not wanting to lose his Confidant to a Swords, Rietzl used his remaining mana to cast a second [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf).


After some thought, Kibler decided he couldn't afford to take any hits from the Goyfs, choosing to use a Swords to kill one rather than wait for the Confidant. The Confidant came down on the following turn, and began to provide a steady stream of cards to Rietzl. Kibler started to fight back, making a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) of his own and an Elspeth for it to defend. Eventually, Rietzl brought the big guns out, finding a [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). Kibler had a [Vindicate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vindicate) for the Knight, dispatching it and making another Elspeth token before passing the turn.


Every turn that went by cemented Rietzl's advantage. While the incremental advantage gained by Elspeth was good, if Kibler didn't get to ultimate soon, the Confidant was going to provide Rietzl enough tools to get her out of the way. Rietzl made a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). Kibler drew and played a much smaller [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage). When the Pridemage got some Elspeth wings and attacked on the following turn, Rietzl sent it home with a [Maze of Ith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+of+Ith) he fetched up with his Knight.


Kibler's Elspeth had finally reached eight loyalty, so Rietzl had to deal with it. What he found was a [Pernicious Deed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pernicious+Deed) (thanks to a little help from his [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) and a [Horizon Canopy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Horizon+Canopy)). That let him play and cast the Deed for two, wiping away all of Kibler's permanents except Elspeth. With the path clear, Rietzl's [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) pushed through to reduce her loyalty. With virtually all of his permanents gone, Kibler just drew and conceded.


**Paul Rietzl 2 – Brian Kibler 1**




Feature Match Round 5 – Matt Nass vs. Felix Lapan
-------------------------------------------------


*by Brian David-Marshall* 

"Were there no better matches in the whole green flight?" aksed Grand Prix Oakland champion Matt Nass as he sat down for his fifth round feature against Montreal's Felix Lapan, who had won a GP Trial with his innovative deck last night. It was the combination of that deck list and Nass' resume that instigated their trip to the Feature Match area but I did not want to reveal anything about Felix's deck.


"I was not expecting to get a Feature," admitted Lapan who described himself as largely a casual player who has been working on this deck with a friend in the Montreal Legacy community for the past year. The deck features [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order) for [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) but can also win in one turn with multiple ways to tutor into play and subsequently sacrifice [Protean Hulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Protean+Hulk) to loop [Body Double](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Body+Double), Reveilark, and [Mogg Fanatic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Fanatic) to his heart's content.


"This was the best there was this round," I assured Nass.


"Don't get me wrong," smiled Nass as he shuffled up to play. "I love feature matches!"


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm5Nass.jpg)*Matt Nass*
### Game 1


Lapan kicked off the action -- on the draw -- with [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) into Matt Nass' [Volcanic Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Island). Nass said "Okay" and Lapan named [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). Nass showed him a hand with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), Jace TMS, [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) as the highlights.


Turn two saw [Carrion Feeder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carrion+Feeder) for Lapan and [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor). Nass [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed at the end of the turn. He sacrificed his [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn) and got [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra) to play Sword to Plowshares. Lapan sac'd the Feeder.


Nass untapped to play [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) and fetch [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull).


"Mind if I read that?" asked Nass as Lapan played a land he did not recognize. It was [Phyrexian Tower](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Tower). Lapan used it cast [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for two -- although he only got a one -- into [Xantid Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xantid+Swarm).


Nass made a sour face. He sacrificed two fetch lands on his own turn and tapped out to play [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) bouncing [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor).


Lapan attacked and played [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall). He replayed the Arbor.


"Mind if I read that?" asked Nass. I expect Lapan to get a lot of that today.


Nass bounced the [Xantid Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xantid+Swarm) this time and passed back to Lapan who was play acting though the sequence of what he wanted to happen.


"You need to play a little faster," urged Nass.


Lapan sacrificed his Wall and attempted to play [Pattern of Rebirth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pattern+of+Rebirth) on the [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor). Nass [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)ed. He then had [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep) for the [Xantid Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xantid+Swarm). Lapan passed the turn and Nass made a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) during the end step. He attacked for five and then played another Mystic -- this time fetching [Sword of Body and Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Body+and+Mind). He had three cards in hand when he passed the turn.


Lapan offered [Academy Rector](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Academy+Rector) and Nass [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed into [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) in response.


"Its your turn," frowned Lapan.


Nass played his Sword and equipped it to a Mystic. He attacked and Lapan was up against the wall. It was even worse when Nass used the remaining counter on his Jace to bounce the Arbor setting Lapan back on mana to a point where he could not claw back.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm5Lapan.jpg)*Felix Lapan*
### Game 2


[Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) opened game two for Lapan and revealed [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), Grim lavamancer, [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), and two lands. Lapan played [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise). Nass cracked a fetch and played [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) -- mana denial had worked out well for him in game one after all.


Lapan laid [Carpet of Flowers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carpet+of+Flowers) and was able to make a white mana during his second main phase. He then followed up with [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) and [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage) with a little boost from [Ancient Tomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Tomb)s. Nass Swords'd the Wall and Lavamancered the Bird. Lapan missed an attack with his Pridemage and chided himself.


Nass played [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) for [Sword of Fire and Ice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Fire+and+Ice) and shot [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor) with [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer). Lapan's [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer) was countered with [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep) and Lapan attacked Nass down to 12. Nass had Swords for the Pridemage and waited for Lapan's next end step to deploy the Sword. Meanwhile Lapan had played [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for two mana only to fetch [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall) which had to block the sworded Mystic. He could not play the [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order) he was holding due to knowing that [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) still loomed in Nass' grip.


Nass played Jace and shipped a card to the bottom of Lapan's library.


Lapan -- now able to make two mana off of [Carpet of Flowers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carpet+of+Flowers) played [Reveillark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reveillark). Nass allowed it. He bounced the [Reveillark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reveillark) on his turn and Lapan returned Seer and [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall) to play. [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall) blocked the Swordsperson and then served to scry for one to the Seer. The Seer then went binward when [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) glared at it.


Nass played Thoughtsieze and saw the 'Lark, [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order), and [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) -- he took the Lark.


Lapan drew [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) and played it, drawing [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep) from Nass. There were two cards left in Nass's hand. One of them was [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) and the other was [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order). Lapan attempted to play the Bird and it was countered with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) pitching [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm).


"I was just hoping you did not have two blue cards left," sighed Lapan as he extended the hand to congratulate Matt Nass on winning the match.


"Your deck seems really cool," said Nass who was just happy he never let Lapan have enough mana to let it do any of the scary things it was capable of.


**Final result: Matt Nass defeated Felix Lapan 2 - 0**




Saturday, 6:14 p.m. – Quick Questions
-------------------------------------


*by Brian David-Marshall* 

### What is the most unlikely deck you have seen so far in this tournament?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/qqDurw.jpg)*Caleb Durward*
**Caleb Durward**: *I lost to Reanimator? I don't know, most Legacy decks are fairly likely unless they are a straight brew and I haven't seen any of those*.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/qqBeg.jpg)*Zaiem Beg*
**Zaiem Beg**: *[Hex](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hex)mage Depths is pretty unlikely. It seems pretty poor in an environment full of [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)s.*


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/qqSach.jpg)*AJ Sacher*
**AJ Sacher**: *Its Legacy so you always see crazy stuff. Enchantress?*  
*There is no unlikely in Legacy. Anything could happen in Legacy! I saw some guy playing Dragon Stompy and I was like, "Yup, its Dragon Stompy!"*


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/qqKibl.jpg)*Brian Kibler*
**Brian Kibler**: *I just played against mono-black, artifact infect deck.*  
*I was not expecting to battle against that. When I sat down to play him my opponent said: "You are going to be really amused by this match." I [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize)d him and saw [Necropede](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Necropede). "You're right I am very amused!"*


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/qqBert.jpg)*Alex Bertoncini*
**Alex Bertoncini**: *[Hive Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hive+Mind)! I have seen four or five people playing [Hive Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hive+Mind)! People are [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell)ing it into play on turn two and then playing [Pact of the Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pact+of+the+Titan). Its Legacy where any deck is possible but I saw a bunch of people playing this and thought: "What is going on here?"*


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/qqSpag.jpg)*Nick Spagnolo*
**Nick Spagnolo**: *Team Italia -- Gerard Fabiano's deck. It is red-black-white. It plays [Badlands](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Badlands)! What deck plays [Badlands](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Badlands)?!? It plays [Figure of Destiny](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Figure+of+Destiny), [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach), [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer), and all these cards that do things -- I guess.*



* ### Saturday, 7:43 p.m. – Watch Where you [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep)


*by Nate Price*


![Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mental+Misstep)

Not since [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) had a card received as much hype as [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep), and it's easy to see why. First, it's a new counterspell. Second, it's free. Put those two together and you have one of the most dominating combinations in **Magic**. Look at [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). Both have at various points been completely dominant in the formats in which they were played. Right now, players often refer to different Legacy decks as [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) decks or non-[Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) decks. Designing cards with a more-or-less free mechanic in it requires a careful touch for developers. So far, it appears that it was beautifully executed.


I took a bit of time to sit down with three noteworthy deck designers to get their opinions about the card and its impact on the format and on their deck designs. The three players I talked to all have reputations as excellent deck designers. Conley Woods, now a staple on the Pro Tour, earned his way there mostly with decks of his own design. Using cards like [Raven's Crime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raven%27s+Crime), [Violent Ultimatum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Violent+Ultimatum), and [Serra Ascendant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra+Ascendant), Woods has proven that he is able to deftly navigate any format, often finding avenues to victory often overlooked by most players.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/blog3Sac.jpg)*AJ Sacher*
Caleb Durward first came to my attention, and the larger stage in general, at Grand Prix Columbus last year, when he used a UG Madess deck featuring [Vengevine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vengevine) and [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest) to make Top 8. Since, he's been making more waves on the Starcitygames.com Open Series, with multiple Top 8 finishes. He epitomizes the spirit of the Grinder, battling week after week, often with decks of his own design, pushing himself to the cusp of national community recognition. The third designer I talked to is the perfect example of a person from both worlds. AJ Sacher is a well-known and respected pro player. He is also a regular at the Open Series, grinding away in both the Standard and Legacy portions of the events. He often posts amazing finishes, and has shown a special affinity for the Legacy format.


Nate: When a card like [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep), one that targets a specific set of cards, is in a format, how much does it affect your design process?


Woods: It impacts it a bunch. It has an effect on the format as a whole, and that factors into deck design. Decks like Goblins and Merfolk aren't as good so decks that are worse against those tend to get better. In addition, you have to be more careful about the contents of your own decks. It's the same thing that happened with [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). People started running cards that they wouldn't have played as many of to match the casting costs the format was showing them. This card makes one-drops worse and slows down the format. You have to take that into account.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/blog3Dur.jpg)*Caleb Durward*
Durward: Yeah, I definitely changed things up a bit. I added cards like [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) to my deck. With [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep) out there, I figured things would be a little easier if I could play the [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) and just start with two drops. I like the ability to negate the cards that are trying to negate mine.


Sacher: Um, do you mean beside the fact that you have to play your own [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep)s and that one-drops are worse? (He continued with a smile) Cards like this have a definite impact on design. Before this card came out, I was playing a lot of decks like UR [Stifle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stifle), and those decks find it really hard to deal with [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep). I've been playing BUG since [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep) came out because it doesn't have the same problems. Generally, my deck doesn't mind getting its one drops countered. Decks where that is the case are at a huge advantage. In addition, it has allowed tempo-based decks to become better. When I can still curve out and protect my cards with [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep), it has made what should be a very reactive card into a proactive threat. Another really important thing it has done is improve the cards that are weaker against one-drop spells. Most of them were already good, but they get even better with an essentially free way to protect them.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/blog3Woo.jpg)*Conley Woods*
Nate: Do you feel that [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep) has lived up to the hype that surrounded its release?


Woods: Yes and no. It's definitely a powerful card, but I think it's already worse than people thought it was going to be. Since people were so on top of its release, it was easy to start building decks to combat it from the beginning. In addition, most people will just buy straight into the hype and start every deck with an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) "4 [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep)," which I think is a mistake and makes the card worse.


Durward: Oh definitely. The card has impacted the format on all levels, from individual card value, to deck design, to the strength of a deck in the format. I would call that worth the hype. I don't think it's quite as good as people thought it was going to be, but it's close.


Sacher: Yeah, but I don't know how long that's going to last. I think this is going to be a card that at some point evens out, and some decks may stop playing it, or at least drop the number of them played. As the decks become slower and more controlling, the card becomes worse. Eventually, it becomes so bad that people stop playing it. At this point, the decks that it beat, like Goblins, are fast enough to beat the slower, more controlling decks. At this point, the blue decks speed up again and [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Mental%2BMisstep) comes back. It's the cycle of the metagame. Right now, I think the best barometer for the power level of the card is the number of Jace, the Mind Scupltors decks play. The higher the number, the worse it is. Jace is the first step in the slowing down process, so I'd keep an eye on it.




Feature Match Round 8 – Anthony Eason vs. Drew Levin
----------------------------------------------------


*by Brian David-Marshall* 

Anthony Eason burst onto the **Magic** scene last year when he earned the chance to represent the USA at Worlds in Chiba as a National team member. The St. Louis native may not have much experience playing Legacy but he found himself with only one loss with just two rounds to go playing a black-white deck descended from the likes of Chris Pikula's Deadguy Ale that took second during the firts ever Legacy GP.


Drew Levin has yet to make his mark on the Pro Tour or trod upon the road to Worlds but he has made quite the name for himself in the Star City Open events posting Top 8 finishes on Standard Saturdays and Legacy Sundays. He recently made his mark on the elder format when he and Gerry Thompson both made the Top 8 in Orlando by resurrecting the [Standstill](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Standstill) archetype when they realized that [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep) meant the deck would have an answer to back breaking turn one plays like [Aether Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aether+Vial) and [Goblin Lackey](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Lackey) -- cards which had made the deck untenable to play. He was playing blue-white this week with [Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision)s and [Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction).


### Game 1


There were mulligans on both sides of the table before Eason led off by cracking a [Marsh Flats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marsh+Flats) and played [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy).


"Two life," announced Drew as he reached for his [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep) to counter it. Then he had a moment of regret. "I don't know if you even know what I am playing."


"I played next to you for the last couple of hours," laughed Eason.


Leving suspended [Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision)s and waited for his investment to pay off. Meanwhile Eason played a turn two [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte). The two players played the waiting game with Eason sitting on a pair of [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)s band Levin waiting until it was absolutley neccessary to fetch.


Eason played [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and drew a frown from Levin who [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed and then let it resolve. He broke a land to shuffle away the dross and filled up his hand. Eason was able to equip his Bob and attack the next turn. Eason imprinted [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) on [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) and played [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) for [Sword of Fire and Ice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Fire+and+Ice).


"I got a good one for you," grinned Levin when Eason ended his turn.


Levin played the oldie-but-still-very-goodie [Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction) and offered Eason a selection of Jace TMS, [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare), [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep), [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm8Eas.jpg)*Anthony Eason*
Eason put Jace and [Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misstep) in one pile and Levin took it despite having to pass on [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares). Levin then played Jace and bounced the [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Eason moved the Jitte onto the Mystic and attacked Jace but Levin had another Swords. Eason replayed [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) only to have Levin play [Vedalken Shackles](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vedalken+Shackles) and take it.


Eason attempted to [Vindicate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vindicate) the Jace but it was met with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). Eason used his remaining Jitte counter to kill the Confidant.


Levin followed up with [Crucible of Worlds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crucible+of+Worlds) and returned a fetch land to play from his bin. Levin began pounding him with quick jabs -- [Repeal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Repeal)[Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox), Fatesealing -- and the game limped on for a couple more turns until Eason finally had enough and they moved on.


### Game 2


Eason led off with a turn one [Bitterblossom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bitterblossom) after imprinting [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) on a [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox). Levin suspended [Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision)s. Eason followed with [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) for Levin's [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra) and [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) for [Sword of Fire and Ice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Fire+and+Ice).


Levin [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed and played [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and braced to take seven from Eason's team once the Sword was deployed. Eason played a second Mystic and with the threat of Battered Skulls looming and no time to find answers to what was already on the board Levin reached for his sideboard.


"That was a good [Bitterblossom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bitterblossom)."


### Game 3


The two players chatted about the Legacy format and Levin admitted that he expected Eason to be playing a red deck -- that was the Standard archetype Eason used to burn his way onto the National team last year.


"I don't know much about this format but it seems like whenever I play a turn two Bob or Stoneforge this deck just wins," said Eason of his choice to play black-white.


"Or turn one," nodded Levin who led off with Celestial Collonade.


Eason played Cabal Therpay naming [Counterspell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterspell). He hit and also saw Swords, [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) and [Repeal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Repeal) along with some lands. The threat of the aforementioned loss to a turn two Stoneforge prompted Levin to pitch his remaining blue cards to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) the ubiquitous critter.


Levin played [Aura of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aura+of+Silence) and Eason gave it a good read. He played [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) but it only drew a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) from Levin. A turn later Eason's next Mystic resolved and earned him a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) for his efforts.


"That was good," smirked Levin as he peeled a card off ther top of his deck and played [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) to bounce the Mystic -- Eason was jammed up on only two lands. Eason replayed the Mystic, this time getting [Sword of Fire and Ice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Fire+and+Ice). He had eight cards in hand and had to discard Jitte.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm8Lev.jpg)*Drew Levin*
Swords bobbed to the top for Levin to dispatch the Mystic and he suspended [Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision)s. Eason played [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) and missed but saw the last card in Levin's grip was [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare). Levin fatesealed and left Thoughtsieze on top. He held up his lone card as Eason drew for the turn. "You want it? You can have it."


Eason paid two life, cast the Thoughtsieze, and took it. He shrugged:


"I am not losing to damage anyway."


Levin could barely contain himself until Eason's next end step after drawing [Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction). Eason resolved [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) but the game was sllipping away. [Visions](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Visions) was about to resolve and Levin got the fat side of a four-one FoF split that Eason arranged to keep his oppoinent from Swords. Levin drew one anyway when Vision resolved and he suspended another for good measure.


Eason had to pay two extra to even try playing a [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) -- that [Aura of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aura+of+Silence) still loomed -- and Levin was so flush with cards he was able to pitch [Misdirection](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misdirection) to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) it. A turn later Elspeth joined his team and that was enough for Eason to give in to the inevitability of the situation.


"Well we played one real game," said Levin.


"I had two [Vindicate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vindicate)s and two lands in my opening hand," said Eason with a shrug of his shoulders.


"[Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction) was just as good as I wanted it to be," said Levin basking in the feeling of climbing back into a game on the back of overwhelming card advantage. "It feels like this is such a grindy format right now.


**Final result: Drew Levin defeated Anthony Eason 2 -1**




Feature Match Round 9 – David Williams vs. David Price
------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

With a loss and a draw, both Williams and Price were in need of a win here to continue playing in the morning. Williams has been a staple around the feature match area for close to as long as it has existed. He has shown an affinity in recent years for older formats, taking part in the Vintage Championship at Gen Con every year, and always making the trip out to a domestic Legacy Grand Prix. His opponent, David Price, isn't as well-known as Williams (as he said when asked by Willians, "No, I'm not that David Price"), but he has had the most recent Magical success. He's coming hot off a Top 16 performance at the starcitygames.com Open Series in Louisville, where he played [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide). This time around, he opted for a deck on the other end of the spectrum: Zoo.


### Game 1


Price threw his opening hand back, but kept an aggressive six-carder. His first-turn [Wild Nacatl](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wild+Nacatl) fell to the card du jour, [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep). His second one fell to a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). He was able to stick a [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer), though, and his offense was going to at least have to start with him. The [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) that he played on the next turn resolved, though Williams did try to dig for an answer with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm9Pri.jpg)*David Price*
Williams had used a pair of [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s to help sift through his deck, but hadn't made anything to really help him. Price was starting to amass an army, and Williams did all he could to slow him down. He used a [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare) on a [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage), but a second resolved. Price waited for a turn to attack with his Knight, choosing to grow it a little more. He also used his Lavamancer when he had three creatures in his graveyard, making sure to keep one around for any potential [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)s. Once the knight started attacking, things went quickly for Williams. With no [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to remove the enormous creature, Williams conceded after a couple of turns.


David Williams 0 – David Price 1


### Game 2


Both players kept their opening draws. Williams made the first blow, using a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) to snag a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull). Price responded deftly with a [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage), preempting the powerful new equipment. This time, it was Williams who preempted Price, shutting down his Pridemage with a [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle). At that point, things got interesting. Williams had two mana available when Price cast [Choke](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Choke). After a moment of thought, Williams decided to use his Mystic to put [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) into play. With his [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s locked down, Williams rebuild with a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and a [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest). Price, meanwhile, built his defenses with a 3/3 [Wild Nacatl](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wild+Nacatl) and a 1/2 [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). A second Pridemage hit the table, and his defense suddenly turned into an offense. He swung his now 5/5 Nacatl into Williams. Williams used his [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to destroy Price's lone [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga). When Price floated a red mana, Williams took the four damage.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gppro11/fm9Wil.jpg)*David Williams*
On Price's turn, he aimed a [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) at the [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull), killing it and making his [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) a 3/4. Price swung. Williams's life was dropping rapidly. A mere turn later, he was facing an alpha strike from Price while at six life. He used his [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) to fetch up a [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra). In response to Williams activating the Rainforest, Price tried to [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) the Mystic, but Williams tapped himself out again to play a [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep). With his new white mana, Williams used a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to kill the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). All the gesture did was buy him one more turn. After drawing his card, he wasted no time before conceding and wishing Price good luck the next day.


**David Williams 0 – David Price 2**
